the-dump 2019-10-09 16:37:12 Superidra_alt
1.  - Use the /g command to launch the game.  2.  Play around with the different settings.  Don't go full-auto.  Try not to use FOMM.  Try to use a single texture with the same size everywhere.  Use a texture resolution of at least 1024x1024 if you can. I like to go with 1024x1024.  When you're finished, exit the game and open the launcher again. If you are lucky enough to be able to run it normally (like I often get) you usually only need to change a single setting, but when you run the game it may take a few minutes to load the map again.  Then you need to use the F6 key, which may require you to restart the game.  Then you need to change the settings again until the map loads.  Then you just need to quit and try again.  The process of loading the map could take from two minutes to several hours.
3.  -
the-dump 2019-10-09 16:37:48 Superidra_alt
step 1. Open up your game directory and load up the new game. This is just a step to get the game running at the right speed.
Note to Skyrim developers: this is a HUGE STEP. If you wish to change what you see in-game, you need to make a backup of your save games. To save your game in Skyrim, open up the Skyrim.ini file located in your skyrim game directory.
When you open the file, make the following changes:
1) Put the following line under [General]
gamebundles.useVanilla=1
2) Add the following line under [System]
d3d9ex.EnableDepthOfField=1
3) After that, save and close the file.
4) Open up any mod that you want to include, make another copy of the mod and use that copy as a source of textures and meshes for Bifrost.
5) Open up the Bifrost .nif file found in your game directory with an image editing program such as Paint Shop Pro
